## 2026-04-09 — Session 4: Architecture Review, Data Validation, Framework Overhaul

**Done**

- Identified ClinicalTrials.gov API for FDA strategy (free, no auth, structured trial data)
- Produced `outputs/development_analysis.docx` — full time estimates + architecture comparison
- Overhauled scoring system: expanded from 5 to 7 dimensions (added Liquidity, Catalyst Timeline)
- Established three-stage signal pipeline: Triage → Scoring → Deep Dive
- Set minimum market cap floor at $300M
- Changed reporting cadence from weekly to daily
- Rewrote INSTRUCTIONS.md with hybrid architecture (Python tools + Claude sessions)
- Updated all 5 strategy specs with validated data sources + deep dive analysis checklists
- Created `framework/candidate_template.md` — standardized candidate writeup template
- Updated CONTEXT.md with validated API reference table
- Updated INDEX.md with new file inventory
- Re-ordered ESMA implementation priority by data accessibility: BaFin → FCA → CNMV

**Decisions**
- Hybrid architecture: Python tools for data collection, Cowork sessions for analysis
- ~~Lambda Finance API~~ → Quiver Quantitative API for Congressional trading (Lambda DNS blocked from sandbox)
- OpenFIGI for cross-strategy entity resolution
- Common JSON signal format across all tools
- Daily reporting cadence
- $300M minimum market cap
- 7-dimension scoring (max 42.5 + convergence bonus up to +8)
- Score thresholds: 30+ Immediate, 22-29 Watchlist, 14-21 Archive, <14 Discard
- ESMA phased by data accessibility: BaFin (CSV) → FCA (structured) → CNMV (HTML)
- Tools output to `signals/` directory; sessions read signals for analysis
- ~~SAM.gov API key registration~~ → Replaced by USAspending.gov (no key needed)

## 2026-04-09 — Session 5: End-to-End Feasibility Testing + File Updates

**Done**
- Ran live API/data tests for all 5 strategies from the Cowork sandbox
- Discovered yfinance Python library solves market cap triage (Yahoo Finance v7/v10 REST APIs now require auth, but the library works without auth for US and UK stocks)
- Discovered openFDA API (`api.fda.gov/drug/drugsfda.json`) as verified data source for drug approval history
- Replaced Lambda Finance with Quiver Quantitative (Lambda DNS blocked; Quiver is richer with ExcessReturn metrics)
- Replaced SAM.gov with USAspending.gov (no API key needed, eliminates 1-4 week wait)
- Confirmed ClinicalTrials.gov API v2 works (use `query.term` not `filter.phase`)
- Identified PDUFA calendar limitation: no clean API exists (FDA.gov 404, biopharmawatch JS-rendered)
- Identified EDGAR tool field name errors (uses `entity_id` which doesn't exist; correct: `ciks[0]`, `adsh`)
- Identified congress.gov API limitation (slow XML, need static committee lookup table)
- Updated all strategy specs, CONTEXT.md, and INSTRUCTIONS.md with feasibility findings
- Added yfinance + openpyxl + pandas to required dependencies

**Feasibility Results (all 5 strategies)**

| Strategy | Status | Blockers |
|----------|--------|----------|
| 1. EDGAR Keyword Scanning | ✅ FULLY FEASIBLE | Existing tool needs refactoring (wrong field names), but API works perfectly |
| 2. ESMA Short Aggregation | ✅ FULLY FEASIBLE | FCA XLSX verified (579 rows), OpenFIGI ISIN→ticker works, yfinance market cap works for .L stocks |
| 3. Congressional Trading | ✅ FULLY FEASIBLE | Quiver Quant returns 1000 trades with return metrics. Committee cross-ref needs static lookup table |
| 4. Contract Awards | ✅ FULLY FEASIBLE | USAspending.gov award queries, size/date filtering, contractor matching all work. yfinance provides revenue for materiality |
| 5. FDA PDUFA Calendar | ⚠️ FEASIBLE WITH CAVEAT | ClinicalTrials.gov + openFDA work. PDUFA calendar tracking has no clean API — needs WebSearch + manual curation |

**Decisions**
- yfinance is the market cap triage tool (replaces Yahoo Finance REST APIs which now need auth)
- openFDA added to data sources for FDA strategy
- ESMA priority corrected: FCA (XLSX, verified) → Bundesanzeiger (HTML, needs parsing) → CNMV (403, needs browser automation)
- Lambda Finance fully replaced by Quiver Quantitative in all docs
- SAM.gov fully replaced by USAspending.gov in all docs
- PDUFA calendar will use semi-manual approach (WebSearch + curated JSON watchlist)
- Committee cross-reference will use static lookup table (not real-time congress.gov API)

## 2026-04-09 — Session 7: Session Continuity Protocol + Max-Usage Rules

**Done**
- Created `SESSION_STATE.md` — the relay baton file. Overwritten (not appended) at end of every session. Contains: current phase, last completed work, in-progress items, next actions, active warnings, active blockers, dependency install commands. New sessions read this first for fastest possible cold-start orientation.
- Updated `INSTRUCTIONS.md` with:
  - New Cold Start Protocol: SESSION_STATE.md is now Step 1 (was previously PROGRESS_LOG)
  - New Session Rules: split into Start/During/End phases with explicit shutdown protocol
  - New "Scheduled Session Behavior" section: no-human-present rules, fail-forward, dependencies reset
  - Max-usage rule: work until limit, but never sacrifice handoff quality for volume
- Updated `project_instructions_for_box.md` with 3 new sections:
  - Section 8: Session Continuity Protocol (cold-start read order + shutdown protocol)
  - Section 9: Maximum Utilization Rule (work until limit, hierarchy: handoff > quality > volume)
  - Section 10: Scheduled Session Behavior (autonomous operation rules)
  - Updated Section 7 (Autonomous Execution) for unattended session context
- Updated `README.md` cold-start instructions to reflect SESSION_STATE as primary read
- Updated `INDEX.md` to show SESSION_STATE as first read item, PROGRESS_LOG moved to Reference
- Updated `OPEN_QUESTIONS.md` with Q-005 (PROGRESS_LOG growth management)

**Decisions**
- SESSION_STATE.md is overwritten, not appended — it's always-current state, not history. PROGRESS_LOG remains append-only history.
- PROGRESS_LOG demoted from "Session Start" to "Reference" in read order. New sessions should never need to read history to know current state.
- Handoff quality > output quality > output volume — explicit hierarchy prevents sessions from running into the wall without saving

- D-011: Web research is mandatory for all candidates (30+ and Watchlist), not optional. Rationale: structured data sources don't capture market narrative — web research bridges the gap and can reveal kill conditions invisible in filings/disclosures.

## 2026-04-09 — Session 9: Concurrency Lock + Scheduled Task Setup

**Done**
- Designed and implemented file-based concurrency lock mechanism (`SESSION_LOCK.md`) to prevent simultaneous scheduled sessions from corrupting project state
- Updated `INSTRUCTIONS.md`: concurrency check as Step 1 of cold start, lock deletion as Step 5 of shutdown, SESSION_LOCK in folder structure, concurrency lock in scheduled session behavior
- Updated `INDEX.md`: SESSION_LOCK.md as first check item in Session Start table
- Updated `SESSION_STATE.md`: concurrency lock added to Active Warnings
- Added decision D-012 to `DECISIONS.md` (file-based concurrency lock rationale and alternatives rejected)
- Created `PROJECT_INSTRUCTIONS.md` — final version of project instructions text with lock mechanism in sections 8 and 10
- Created `scheduled_task_prompt_v2.md` — complete scheduled task prompt with Phase 0 (concurrency check), Phase 1 (orient), Phase 2 (determine work mode), Phase 3 (execute), Phase 4 (shutdown)
- All project files now consistently reference the lock mechanism

**Decisions**
- D-012: File-based SESSION_LOCK.md with 4-hour staleness timeout. Creates at startup, deletes at shutdown. Stale locks (>4hrs) are overridden to prevent deadlock from crashed sessions. Interactive sessions skip the lock check.
- Scheduled session frequency: hourly (Cowork only supports hourly/daily/weekly). Concurrency lock ensures bounced sessions cost almost nothing (one file read then stop).

**Next** (pending Pedro's approval — see `OPEN_QUESTIONS.md` Q-001)

3. Pedro approves build start (Q-001)
4. First build session: OpenFIGI module → EDGAR refactor → Congressional client

**⚠️ Key Issue: Workspace Sandbox Lock**
- Running the EDGAR scanner exceeded the 45s bash timeout, locking the workspace sandbox for the remainder of Session 14
- The sandbox enters a "process already running" state that persists indefinitely within the session
- New sessions get fresh sandboxes, so this is transient — but it killed ~60% of Session 14's productive execution time
- Mitigations applied: subprocess isolation (D-014), individual scanner scripts (run_scanner.py), wall-clock budget (EDGAR v2.1)
- See Q-007 in OPEN_QUESTIONS.md for full analysis

**🔄 In Progress**
- First integrated scan: could not be completed due to workspace lock (3 signals successfully collected from Capitol Trades before lock)

### 📝 Process Lesson

For any FDA catalyst candidate, **Flag 2 (clinical data quality — ITT vs mITT, endpoint-miss magnitude, secondary endpoint strength) MUST be verified before any preliminary score > 28 is assigned**. The Session 23 MNKD prelim was built on an assumption about what the selloff was caused by (Tyvaso overhang decoupled from Afrezza catalyst) without validating the underlying INHALE-1 trial result. The adversarial review this session caught the gap. This matches the project-instruction hierarchy: "first correct, then creative, then elegant."

## Session 49 (Interactive) — 2026-04-13 — Date Correction

### ⚠️ CRITICAL ERROR CORRECTED: April 13, 2026 day-of-week

**Error**: Starting from approximately Session 16 (the TVTX candidate file update), April 13, 2026 was incorrectly labeled as a **Sunday**. It is actually a **Monday**. This error propagated across 15+ files including SESSION_STATE.md, the main TVTX candidate file, daily reports, and 8 working session files.

**Root cause**: A prior session's calendar computation was wrong, and no subsequent session verified the day-of-week claim — each one copied the "Sunday" label from existing files.

**Downstream impact assessment**:
- The error caused incorrect reasoning about FDA timing (e.g., "FDA doesn't issue on weekends, so expect Friday April 11 or Monday April 14"). Since April 13 IS a Monday (a normal business day), the FDA could issue the decision on April 13 itself.
- The error did NOT cause any missed trade signals or bad position decisions — the TVTX position was already established, and monitoring sessions correctly checked for decisions regardless of the day-of-week label.
- The "expect Friday early decision" reasoning was partially wrong in its motivation (it was based on the "PDUFA falls on weekend" pattern) but the action (check Friday) was still reasonable as FDA can release early.

**Files corrected**: SESSION_STATE.md, TVTX_FSGS_PDUFA.md, PROGRESS_LOG.md, 2026-04-13_S48_daily_report.md, and 8 working/session*_tvtx*.md files.

**Lesson**: Day-of-week claims must be programmatically verified, never assumed from prior session notes. Added to feedback memory.

### Self-Review
- **Accuracy check**: All price data verified via yfinance live API calls. TVTX decision checked via 5 independent sources. All scanner results verified.
- **Logic check**: TVTX web snippets showing $36-38 prices are suggestive but not conclusive without confirmed timestamps. Correctly classified as INCONCLUSIVE rather than jumping to conclusion.
- **Completeness check**: All S43 priority items addressed. Added value: PDUFA pipeline data quality review, future candidate flagging (SRRK, SVRA, CAPR).
- **Adversarial check**: Could the $38.21 web snippet be from a different time? Yes — the "above 10-year high $37.04" could reference any breakout above that level. Without confirmed Apr 14 date, treating as unverified is correct.
- **Data freshness check**: yfinance data current through Apr 10 only. Apr 14 (Monday) data was not available at time of query (~10:00 UTC, before US market close). S44 will have complete Monday data.

## S46 Interactive — 2026-04-13: Full System Audit + 12 Bug Fixes + 4 File Truncation Repairs

**Context**: User requested comprehensive system audit ("check every single line data point"). Discovered 12 findings across 3 severity levels plus 4 file truncation bugs. All resolved.

### ✅ Completed

1. **Schedule changed** (D-048): Operational task from `0 9 * * 1-5` to `0 */3 * * *`. Maintenance task from `0 6 * * 1-5` to `50 */3 * * *`. Both now run every 3 hours, every day including weekends.

2. **ESMA scanner fix**: Removed duplicate trailing code (lines 671-679).

3. **EDGAR monitor fixes** (v2.3→v2.4): Fixed `signals_dir` parameter bug in main() (would crash on direct CLI invocation); deduplicated rotation logic in main() to call `get_next_rotation_category()` instead of reimplementing; standardized datetime from `utcnow()` to `now()`.

4. **PDUFA watchlist cleanup**: Tagged XSPRAY.ST, 6446.TW, EGTX as `non_tradeable` (non-US exchanges); tagged ACLX as `linked_to_GILD` (duplicate of GILD anito-cel entry). Confirmed IONS×2, RARE×2, MNKD×2 are NOT duplicates — different drugs, same company.

5. **Convergence engine improvements**: Added `governance_keyword` to BEARISH_PATTERNS; added `contract_new_award`, `contract_modification`, `congressional_trade` to BULLISH_PATTERNS. Reduces neutral fallthrough.

6. **Convergence file cleanup**: Added `cleanup_old_convergence_files()` to `run_post_scan.py` — removes convergence_*.json files older than 7 days.

7. **run_scanner.py**: Fixed help text from "$300M" to "$215M" market cap filter.

8. **INSTRUCTIONS.md overhaul**: Updated tool versions (EDGAR v2.4, contract v1.1, FDA v2.0); fixed contradictory lock instructions ("delete" → "overwrite with UNLOCKED"); added Scheduled Tasks section documenting both tasks; corrected "hourly" → "every 3 hours, every day".

9. **OPEN_QUESTIONS.md**: Updated Q-004 schedule reference to reflect new cron and maintenance task.

10. **FILE TRUNCATION REPAIRS** — discovered 4 Python files truncated on disk:
    - `convergence_engine.py`: 510 lines on disk, should be 558. Cut mid-statement at `with open(report_file, "w"`. Missing entire CLI section.
    - `congressional_trading.py`: 715 lines, should be 736. Cut at `signals = run_full_scan(\n        d`.
    - `contract_monitor.py`: 493 lines, should be 533. Cut at `parser.add_argument("--dry-run"... h`.
    - `fda_pdufa_pipeline.py`: 931 lines, should be 955. Cut at `print(f"  {d['ticker']:6s} | {d['c`.
    All fixed by appending missing tail code via bash. Root cause: prior session Write operations were cut short (likely context pressure or size limits). The Read tool's in-memory cache showed full content, masking the disk truncation. Only detectable via py_compile in the bash sandbox.

11. **Full compilation verification**: All 15 Python tools in tools/ compile clean via py_compile.
